### Post by jw37 on 2010-12-01
Hello! I have a major problem: Ubuntu is not starting at all anymore.
 
I have used the 32 bit Ubuntu 10.04 for over a half a year without any (serious) problems. The harware has been the same all the time. The problem came up after the latest update. I really do not remember what packages I updated.
 
On startup this message appears:
 
"Ubuntu is running in low-graphics mode. Your screen, graphics card, and input devices could not be detected correctly. You will need to configure these yourself."
 
Click Ok and a dialog appears:
 
"What would you like to do?
 
1) Run Ubuntu in low-graphics mode for just on session
2) Reconfigure graphics
3) Trobleshoot the error
4) Exit to console login
5) Restart X"
 
Option  1: Something that reminds startup happens, but soon the comp freezes. You can only reboot.
 
Option 2: You cannot choose any of the further options given! Or you can select any but clicking Ok does not do anything!
 
Option 3: There's a lot of text that says nothing to me, and I cannot copy-paste it here (I'm now writing in Windows; thank god it's still installed). What should I see in these texts?
 
Option 4: I can successfully login to console but don't know what to do there.
 
Option 5: No good.
 
 
I have already tried: Boot on recovery mode and repair broken packages. Didn't help.
 
 
Help is needed indeed. I hope you experts can advise me, please :-]

---

### Post by ENigma885 on 2010-12-05
Do u have any Xorg PPAs enabled?

### Post by jw37 on 2010-12-06
Well I looked at

/etc/apt/sources.list
/etc/apt/sources.list.d/

and saw no traces of xorg. Does this mean that no xorg ppa is enabled? On the other hand, there are hundreds of files containing 'xorg' in filename.

I don't even know whether this xorg is an essential part of graphical interface of the operating system or some extra stuff. [http://www.x.org/wiki/](http://www.x.org/wiki/)  Anyway I didn't know that such a thing exists.

I have noticed that many people have this kind of problems. I wonder why there isn't a sticky thread or some other big note about how to fix these errors.

---

### Post by ENigma885 on 2010-12-06
> **jw37 said:**
> Thanks for answering. I would definitely like someone to help me, if I were in ur place. =) 

> **jw37 said:**
> How do I find out that?
Of course if u mess around usually with adding PPAs to ur repositories, there's a high probability that u have lots of PPAs enabled and u don't even remember u added them neither are u aware that their packages appear in updates. 

_SO, let's see what u have in ur source list;_
**1-** Open "/etc/apt/sources.list" with a text editor, like gedit, and copy its contents and paste them here wrapped between CODE tags like [PHP]```
SOURCE.LIST CONTENTS
```[/PHP]
**2-** Open a terminal window (*Applications>>Accessories>>Terminal*), paste ```
ls -a '/etc/apt/sources.list.d'
``` and copy the outcome here like what u did above.

> **jw37 said:**
>  how to disable them?
it's not about disabling them. If u have them enabled, the packages are already installed in ur system. So, we will replace them with the official Ubuntu packages with a small trick.

---

### Post by ENigma885 on 2010-12-07
The repositories seem extra fine. That's y I suggest we turn to the starting point;
> **jw37 said:**
> ... The problem came up after the latest update. I really do not remember what packages I updated.

**-** What kind of update? u mean upgraded from 10.04 to 10.10? or just installed the updates offered in 10.04?
**-** If it's the later, we can see what packages were updated by checking the dpkg, Debian package management system, history. In this case u r supposed to attach (*/var/log/dpkg.log*) and any sequences of it like dpkg.log1 and dpkg.log2 if present in the same folder. 
**-** Another thing, the post was posted 5 days ago i.e on Tuesday 2/12. Was it the same day the problem appeared?
**-** ALSO, an important thing I have to mention; I really doubt that an officially released update can cause such problem. Even if it did, a fix should have been released. So, check if there's any updates available by now.
```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade
```

---

```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade
```

### Post by ENigma885 on 2010-12-08
So, the problem was that ur system was starting only in the low graphics mode.
> **jw37 said:**
> On startup this message appears:
 "Ubuntu is running in low-graphics mode. Your screen, graphics card, and input devices could not be detected correctly. You will need to configure these yourself." 

And after the update u can actually reach the login window, but when u enter ur password it reappears again.
> **jw37 said:**
> I did that, and now I'm asked to login (a graphical window), but all that happens is that the login window appears again. I tried many times (carefully to enter the correct password). Normally, I'm logged in automatically.
- No errors appear??
The only case, as far as I know, the login window reappears again after entering the password is when u enter a wrong one.
In this case, it's an easy task to recover ur password;
**1-** Enter the recovery mode from the boot menu (it's called GRUB menu btw)
the option will appear like ```
Ubuntu, with Linux X.X.XX-XX-generic (recovery mode)
``` were those Xs are the kernel version. Just click on it!
**2-** Choose root
**3-** Now u r in a root shell. Type
```
passwd YOURUSERNAME
```were "YOURUSERNAME" is the user name u used to login with. Enter and reenter a new password. U should see something like "password updated successfully"
**4-** Then reboot by
```
reboot -f
```

Honestly, you are confusing me!! : )
correct me if i am wrong about the sequence:
**1-** Some updates were installed that caused ur system to start in Safe Mode. That's when u posted ur problem here.
**2-** U started in Safe Mode and installed the most recent updates by ```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade
```
**3-** After the updates were installed u could reach the login window but it does not accept ur password.
**4-** You followed the steps i posted to reset ur username password, didn't u?
What happened next?

### Post by ENigma885 on 2010-12-08
mmm...I can assure u that a non-experienced user who has the "install-every-thing-from-wherever desire" is more disastrous than Chernobyl.

Despite of the fact that I am totally sure that changing a user's pw cannot affect ur system any further than a pw change; meaning that it cannot be the reason behind the boot problem recurrence, I recommend that u simply fresh-install as long as there's noting to lose except for a couple of minutes to reinstall.
